3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
```

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Rust-Servo Shared Style System Discovery

## Your Task

The Rust compiler and Servo browser engine share code via common Rust crates. Find: 1. In `servo/servo`: the Cargo.toml files under `components/style/` and `components/selectors/` that define the `style` and `selectors` crates — report each crate's declared dependencies. 2. In `servo/servo`: the main entry point file for the style system (`components/style/lib.rs`). 3. In `rust-lang/rust`: find if any crate under `compiler/` or `library/` depends on or shares code with Servo's `selectors` crate (search for `selectors` in Cargo.toml files). 4. In `rust-lang/rust`: the file that defines the `proc_macro` bridge which Servo build scripts use. Report each file path and the key dependency or symbol.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out. Use Sourcegraph MCP tools to explore the codebase.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/rust--01f6ddf7` (rust-lang/rust)
- `sg-evals/servo--be6a2f99` (servo/servo)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

75-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed the discovery task and created `/workspace/answer.json` with comprehensive findings about the shared code between Rust and Servo's style systems.

## Summary of Key Discoveries:

**1. Servo's Style System (servo/servo)**
- There are **no** `components/style/` or `components/selectors/` directories in Servo
- The style system is entirely external, coming from the separate `https://github.com/servo/stylo` repository at a pinned revision
- All Servo components that need styling depend on workspace-level definitions for `selectors`, `stylo`, and related crates

**2. Rust Compiler Dependencies**
- The Rust compiler's `compiler/` and `library/` crates do **not** depend on Servo's selectors crate
- Rust only tests Servo's selectors through `src/tools/cargotest/main.rs` to verify compatibility

**3. Proc_macro Bridge (Key Shared Infrastructure)**
- Defined in `library/proc_macro/src/bridge/` module
- Core files:
  - `mod.rs` - Bridge API definition using `with_api!` macro
  - `server.rs` - Server-side handle management and traits
  - `client.rs` - Client-side bridge implementation
- This enables Servo's build scripts to use procedural macros that communicate with the Rust compiler

The answer has been written to `/workspace/answer.json` with all relevant files, symbols, and a detailed narrative explanation of the architectural relationships.

Rust Compiler's Relationship with Servo's Selectors\\n\\n**No Direct Dependency**: The Rust compiler's `compiler/` and `library/` crates do NOT depend on or import Servo's `selectors` crate.\\n\\n**Testing Integration**: \\n- `src/tools/cargotest/main.rs` (lines 72-83) includes Servo as a test case\\n- Line 79: `packages: &[\\\"selectors\\\"]` - Tests only the selectors crate from Servo\\n- This is for verification that Servo's selectors package compiles with the Rust compiler being tested\\n\\n### 3. Lines 148-166: Defines `BridgeConfig<'a>` struct for establishing server-client communication\\n  - Includes handle management, RPC encoding/decoding, and API tag definitions\\n\\n- `library/proc_macro/src/bridge/server.rs` - Server-side implementation\\n  - Defines `HandleStore<S: Types>` for managing handles\\n  - Implements encoding/decoding traits for inter-process communication\\n  - Provides server-side traits for proc macro execution\\n\\n- `library/proc_macro/src/bridge/client.rs` - Client-side implementation\\n  - Implements bridge entry points for proc macro clients\\n  - Manages thread-local bridge state via `Bridge::with()`\\n  - Provides methods like `def_site()`, `call_site()`, etc.\\n\\n**Key Dependency**: The bridge uses a closed-channel design with handle-based serialization to safely interface between two copies of `proc_macro` built by different compilers (e.g., stage0/bin/rustc vs stage1/bin/rustc during bootstrap).\\n\\n### Architectural Summary\\n\\nThe shared code between Rust and Servo follows a clear separation:\\n1. **Servo** depends on external styling crates from `servo/stylo` repository\\n2. **Rust compiler** does not depend on these crates directly but can test compatibility via cargotest\\n3. **Proc_macro bridge** is a Rust standard library component that enables build scripts and proc macros to communicate with the compiler, which Servo uses for its build system\\n\\nThis architecture allows Rust and Servo to share styling infrastructure (through the separate stylo repository) while maintaining independence - the Rust compiler itself doesn't need to import the selectors crate, but projects like Servo can use it for CSS selector matching.\"\n}\n",
